<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2011._%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8B_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%B2_%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B5_174.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/2011._%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8B_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%B2_%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B5_174.jpg/220px-2011._%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8B_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%B2_%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B5_174.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/2011._%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8B_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%B2_%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B5_174.jpg/330px-2011._%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8B_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%B2_%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B5_174.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/2011._%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8B_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%B2_%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B5_174.jpg/440px-2011._%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8B_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%B2_%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B5_174.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2976" data-file-height="1984" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2011._%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8B_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%B2_%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B5_174.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Children's Day in <a href="/wiki/Donetsk" title="Donetsk">Donetsk</a>, Ukraine, 2011</div></div></div>
<p>Children's Day began on the second Sunday of June in 1857 by Reverend Dr. Charles Leonard, pastor of the Universalist Church of the Redeemer in <a href="/wiki/Chelsea,_Massachusetts" title="Chelsea, Massachusetts">Chelsea, Massachusetts</a>: Leonard held a special service dedicated to, and for the children. Leonard named the day Rose Day, though it was later named Flower Sunday, and then named Children's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Children's Day was first officially declared a national <a href="/wiki/Holiday" title="Holiday">holiday</a> by the Republic of <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> in 1920 with the set date of 23 April. Children's Day has been celebrated nationally since 1920 with the government and the newspapers of the time declaring it a day for the children. However, it was decided that an official confirmation was needed to clarify and justify this celebration and the official declaration was made nationally in 1929 by the founder and the President of the Republic of <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk" title="Mustafa Kemal Atatürk">Mustafa Kemal Atatürk</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The International Day for Protection of Children is observed in many countries as Children's Day on 1 June since 1950. It was established by the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_International_Democratic_Federation" title="Women&#39;s International Democratic Federation">Women's International Democratic Federation</a> on its congress in <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> (4 November 1949).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Major global variants include a <b>Universal Children's Holiday</b> on 20 November, by <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> recommendation.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Even though Children's Day is celebrated globally by most of the countries in the world (almost 50) on 1 June, 
<b>Universal Children's Day</b> takes place annually on 20 November.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> First proclaimed by the United Kingdom in 1954, it was established to encourage all countries to institute a day, firstly to promote mutual exchange and understanding among children and secondly to initiate action to benefit and promote the welfare of the world's children.
</p><p>That is observed to promote the objectives outlined in the Charter and for the welfare of children.  On 20 November 1959, the United Nations adopted the <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_the_Rights_of_the_Child" title="Declaration of the Rights of the Child">Declaration of the Rights of the Child</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-United_Nations_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-United_Nations-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The United Nations adopted the <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Rights_of_the_Child" title="Convention on the Rights of the Child">Convention on the Rights of the Child</a> on 20 November 1989 and can be found on the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> website.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2000, the Millennium Development Goals outlined by world leaders to stop the spread of HIV/AIDS by 2015. Albeit this applies to all people, the primary objective is concerning children.<sup id="cite_ref-United_Nations_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-United_Nations-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> UNICEF is dedicated to meeting the six of eight goals that apply to the needs of children so that they are all entitled to fundamental rights written in the 1989 international human rights treaty.<sup id="cite_ref-UNICEF_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNICEF-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> UNICEF delivers vaccines, works with policymakers for good health care and education and works exclusively to help children and protect their rights.<sup id="cite_ref-UNICEF_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNICEF-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2012, the Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> of the United Nations led the initiative for the education of children.<sup id="cite_ref-Global_Education_First_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Global_Education_First-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> He firstly wants every child to be able to attend school, a goal by 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Global_Education_First_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Global_Education_First-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Secondly, to improve the skill set acquired in these schools.<sup id="cite_ref-Global_Education_First_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Global_Education_First-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Finally, implementing policies regarding education to promote peace, respect, and environmental concern.<sup id="cite_ref-Global_Education_First_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Global_Education_First-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
Universal Children's Day is not just a day to celebrate children for who they are, but to bring awareness to children around the globe that have experienced violence in forms of abuse, exploitation, and discrimination. Children are used as laborers in some countries, immersed in armed conflict, living on the streets, suffering by differences be it religion, minority issues, or disabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Children feeling the effects of war can be displaced because of the armed conflict and may suffer physical and psychological trauma.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The following violations are described in the term "children and armed conflict": recruitment and <a href="/wiki/Child_soldier" class="mw-redirect" title="Child soldier">child soldiers</a>, killing/maiming of children, abduction of children, attacks on schools/hospitals and not allowing humanitarian access to children.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Currently, there are about 153 million children between the ages of 5 and 14 who are forced into child labor.<sup id="cite_ref-international.gc.ca_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-international.gc.ca-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The International Labour Organization in 1999 adopted the Prohibition and Elimination of the Worst Forms of <a href="/wiki/Child_Labour" class="mw-redirect" title="Child Labour">Child Labour</a> including slavery, child prostitution, and child pornography.<sup id="cite_ref-international.gc.ca_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-international.gc.ca-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A summary of the rights under the Convention on the Rights of the Child can be found on the <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> website.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Canada co-chaired the World Summit for children in 1990, and in 2002 the United Nations reaffirmed the commitment to complete the agenda of the 1990 World Summit. This added to the UN Secretary-General's report <i>We the Children: End-of Decade review of the follow-up to the World Summit for Children</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The United Nations children's agency released a study<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> referencing the population increase of children will make up 90 percent of the next billion people.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dates_around_the_world">Dates around the world</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Dates around the world">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Children%27s+Day%22">"Children's Day"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Children%27s+Day%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Children%27s+Day%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Children%27s+Day%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Children%27s+Day%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Children%27s+Day%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2016</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The officially recognized date of Children's Day varies from country to country. This section lists some significant examples, in order of date of observance.
