<p>In <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, Children's Day is celebrated on 1 June. It was established as a holiday in 1949.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Serbia">Serbia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=69" title="Edit section: Serbia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> Children's Day is celebrated on 20 November, since 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Singapore">Singapore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=70" title="Edit section: Singapore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Traditionally, 1 October is the day which <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> officially celebrates Children's Day. A similar event celebrated every year is <a href="/wiki/Youth_Day" title="Youth Day">Youth Day</a>, which is celebrated on the first Sunday of July every year. Kindergarten and primary school children in Singapore do not have to attend school on this day. From 2011, Children's Day was celebrated on the first Friday of October.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Africa">South Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=71" title="Edit section: South Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, Children's Day is on the first Saturday of November but not really celebrated in any significant way.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Sudan">South Sudan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=72" title="Edit section: South Sudan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, Children's Day is celebrated on 23 December, the birthday of South Sudan's "greatest child" according to tribal mythology.
(4)
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Slovakia">Slovakia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=73" title="Edit section: Slovakia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>, the day is called International Children's Day (<i>Medzinárodný deň detí</i>) and is celebrated on 1 June. Children get free entrance to some attractions like zoos<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=74" title="Edit section: Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, this date is celebrated on the 2nd Sunday of May, and it is called "Día del niño".
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sri_Lanka">Sri Lanka</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=75" title="Edit section: Sri Lanka">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>, Children's Day is celebrated on 1 October, which they call in Sinhala as 'Loka Lama Dinaya'
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sudan">Sudan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=76" title="Edit section: Sudan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, Children's Day is celebrated on 23 December, the birthday of Sudan's "greatest child" according to tribal mythology.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Suriname">Suriname</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=77" title="Edit section: Suriname">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>, Children's Day or <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kinderdag&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kinderdag (page does not exist)">Kinderdag</a><sup class="noprint" style="font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kinderdag" class="extiw" title="nl:Kinderdag">nl</a>&#93;</sup> is celebrated on 5 December. Generally, children up to 12 years old receive presents from their parents.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sweden">Sweden</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=78" title="Edit section: Sweden">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, Children's Day is celebrated on the first Monday of October. It was <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Ros%C3%A9n" title="Gustav Rosén">Gustav Rosén</a> who is credited with starting a Children's Day in <a href="/wiki/Ume%C3%A5" title="Umeå">Umeå</a> in northern Sweden in 1905.<sup id="cite_ref-ohlin_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohlin-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Switzerland">Switzerland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=79" title="Edit section: Switzerland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, Children's day was established as a holiday on 20 November 1925.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taiwan">Taiwan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=80" title="Edit section: Taiwan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background-color:#b0c4de">Children's Day (ROC)</th></tr><tr style="display:none;"><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">Traditional&#160;Chinese</a></th><td><span lang="zh-Hant" style="font-size:1rem;" title="Chinese language text">婦女節、兒童節合併假期</span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><table class="collapsible collapsed" style="padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-size: 100%; text-align: left; background-color: #f9ffbc;">Transcriptions</th></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #dcffc9;"><a href="/wiki/Standard_Chinese" title="Standard Chinese">Standard Mandarin</a></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Hanyu_Pinyin" class="mw-redirect" title="Hanyu Pinyin">Hanyu Pinyin</a></th><td><span style="font-style:normal" lang="zh-Latn" title="Chinese-language romanization">Fùnǚ Jié, Értóng Jié Hébìng Jiàqí</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Wade%E2%80%93Giles" title="Wade–Giles">Wade–Giles</a></th><td><span style="font-style:normal" lang="zh-Latn" title="Chinese-language romanization">Fu<sup>4</sup>-nü<sup>3</sup> Chieh<sup>2</sup>, Erh<sup>2</sup>-t'ung<sup>2</sup> Chieh<sup>2</sup> He<sup>2</sup>-ping<sup>4</sup> Chia<sup>4</sup>-ch'i<sup>2</sup></span></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #dcffc9;"><a href="/wiki/Southern_Min" title="Southern Min">Southern Min</a></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Hokkien" title="Hokkien">Hokkien</a> <a href="/wiki/Pe%CC%8Dh-%C5%8De-j%C4%AB" title="Pe̍h-ōe-jī">POJ</a></th><td><span style="font-style:normal" lang="nan-Latn" title="Taiwanese Hokkien-language romanization">Hū-lí-chiat, Jî-tông-chiat Ha̍p-pèng Ká-kî</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Taiwanese_Romanization_System" title="Taiwanese Romanization System">Tâi-lô</a></th><td><span style="font-style:normal" lang="nan-Latn" title="Taiwanese Hokkien-language romanization">Hū-lí-tsiat, Jî-tông-tsiat Ha̍p-pìng Ká-kî</span></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of China">Republic of China</a></b> on Taiwan designated 4 April as Children's Day (<a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">Chinese</a>&#58; <span lang="zh-Hant"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%85%92%E7%AB%A5%E7%AF%80" class="extiw" title="wikt:兒童節">兒童節</a>; <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>: Értóng Jié</span>), pursuant to Article 5 of the <i>Order to Implement Commemoration Days and Holidays</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The holiday dates back to 1931 and since then schools often hold special activities in order to celebrate the occasion. Because of pressure from parents demanding to accompany their children in the celebration, Taiwan celebrated Women's Day together with Children's Day on 4 April 1991. Since then, 4 April has been known as "The Combined Holidays of Women's Day and Children's Day" (<a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">Chinese</a>&#58; <span lang="zh-Hant"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%A9%A6%E5%A5%B3%E7%AF%80" class="extiw" title="wikt:婦女節">婦女節</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E3%80%81" class="extiw" title="wikt:、">、</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%85%92%E7%AB%A5%E7%AF%80" class="extiw" title="wikt:兒童節">兒童節</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%90%88%E4%BD%B5" class="extiw" title="wikt:合併">合併</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%81%87%E6%9C%9F" class="extiw" title="wikt:假期">假期</a></span>). It has been a public holiday of Taiwan, ROC since 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1931, <a href="/wiki/Kong_Xiangxi" class="mw-redirect" title="Kong Xiangxi">Kong Xiangxi</a> initiated the establishment of the China Association for Charity and Children's Association to propose 4 April as Children's Day. The Executive Yuan stipulated in Article 5 of the "Memorial Day and Festival Implementation Measures" that on 4 April, Children's Day, relevant organs, groups, and schools held celebration activities [2]. A one-day holiday was merged with Women's Day from 1991 to 1997 (formally known as "Women's Day, Children's Day Merger Holiday"). After 1998, the holiday was canceled and it was incorporated into the week of holiday. In 1998, two days before the rest of the week, the children of elementary and junior high school students had a day off. Since 2011, it has returned to the national holiday and the country has a holiday for one day. In 2012, if the law is revised again, if it meets the same day as the Ching Ming Festival, it will be on 3 April of the previous day, and if it is on Thursday, it will be on the following day.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Thailand">Thailand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=81" title="Edit section: Thailand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2012_Children%27s_Day_Chiang_Mai_rifle.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/2012_Children%27s_Day_Chiang_Mai_rifle.JPG/220px-2012_Children%27s_Day_Chiang_Mai_rifle.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/2012_Children%27s_Day_Chiang_Mai_rifle.JPG/330px-2012_Children%27s_Day_Chiang_Mai_rifle.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/2012_Children%27s_Day_Chiang_Mai_rifle.JPG/440px-2012_Children%27s_Day_Chiang_Mai_rifle.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1272" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2012_Children%27s_Day_Chiang_Mai_rifle.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Children's Day 2012 at the <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Mai" title="Chiang Mai">Chiang Mai</a> <a href="/wiki/Royal_Thai_Air_Force" title="Royal Thai Air Force">Royal Thai Air Force</a> base</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> National Children's Day (<a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a>: <span lang="th">วันเด็กแห่งชาติ</span>) is celebrated on the second Saturday in January. Known as "Wan Dek" in Thailand, Children's Day is celebrated to give children the opportunity to have fun and to create awareness about their significant role in the development of the country. It was established as a holiday in 1955.
</p><p>Usually, His Majesty the King gives advice addressing the children while the Supreme Monarch Patriarch of Thailand gives moral teaching. The Prime Minister also usually gives each Children's Day a theme and a slogan.
</p><p>Many Government offices are open to children and their family; this includes the Government House, the Parliament House Complex and various Military installations. These events may include a guided tour and an exhibition. A notable example is the guided tour at the Government House, where children have an opportunity to view the Prime Minister's office and sit at the bureau. The Royal Thai Air Force usually invites children to go and explore the aircraft and the Bangkok Bank distributes stationery, such as pens, pencils, and books to every child that enters the bank as a community service. Many organizations from both the government and commercial sectors have celebration activities for children. Children can enter zoos or ride buses for free.
</p><p>There is a Thai saying that states, "Children are the future of the nation, if the children are intelligent, the country will be prosperous."
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trinidad_and_Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=82" title="Edit section: Trinidad and Tobago">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/International_Men%27s_Day" title="International Men&#39;s Day">International Men's Day</a> on 19 November and celebrates Children's Day on 20 November in <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tobago" title="Tobago">Tobago</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tunisia">Tunisia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=83" title="Edit section: Tunisia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Children's Day in <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a> is celebrated on 11 January every year. It was established as a holiday in 1995. It is a day in which Tunisians observe the rights of children and remind themselves that children are the future builders and developers of the country and the world.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">Turkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=84" title="Edit section: Turkey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:T%C3%BCrkisches_Kinderfest_2007_02.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/T%C3%BCrkisches_Kinderfest_2007_02.JPG/220px-T%C3%BCrkisches_Kinderfest_2007_02.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/T%C3%BCrkisches_Kinderfest_2007_02.JPG/330px-T%C3%BCrkisches_Kinderfest_2007_02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/T%C3%BCrkisches_Kinderfest_2007_02.JPG/440px-T%C3%BCrkisches_Kinderfest_2007_02.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:T%C3%BCrkisches_Kinderfest_2007_02.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"The Holiday of National Sovereignty and Children" (Turkey), celebrated in <a href="/wiki/Turks_in_Germany" title="Turks in Germany">Germany</a>, in 2011</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Grand_National_Assembly_of_Turkey" title="Grand National Assembly of Turkey">Grand National Assembly of Turkey</a> was established on 1920, 23 April, and to commemorate the event, 23 April was proclaimed a national holiday in 1921. Since 1927<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> it has also become Children's Day (<a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i lang="tr">Ulusal Egemenlik ve Çocuk Bayramı</i>, literally "The Holiday of National Sovereignty and Children"), an official holiday dedicated to the children of Turkey and (from 1979 on) the world.
</p><p>In addition to holding many domestic celebratory events such as stadium performances, Turkey also houses <a href="/w/index.php?title=TRT_International_23_April_Children%27s_Festival&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="TRT International 23 April Children&#39;s Festival (page does not exist)">TRT International 23 April Children's Festival</a>, where groups of children from other countries are invited to participate in the festivities while staying at Turkish families' homes.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=85" title="Edit section: Tuvalu">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first Monday in August is National Children's Day in <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>. This public holiday is called in Tuvalu Aso Tamaliki.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ukraine">Ukraine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=86" title="Edit section: Ukraine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2013._%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8B_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B9_040.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/2013._%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8B_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B9_040.jpg/220px-2013._%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8B_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B9_040.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/2013._%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8B_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B9_040.jpg/330px-2013._%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8B_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B9_040.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/2013._%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8B_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B9_040.jpg/440px-2013._%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8B_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B9_040.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2013._%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D1%89%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%8B_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B9_040.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Children's Day in <a href="/wiki/Donetsk" title="Donetsk">Donetsk</a>, in 2013</div></div></div>
<p>Day of Children's Protection (Children's Day) (<a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">День захисту дітей</span>, <i>Den zakhystu ditey</i>, literally "day of children's protection") is celebrated on 1 June. In Ukraine Children's Day is set in accordance with the presidential decree of Ukraine from 30 May 1998 No. 568/98.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Qatar">Qatar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=87" title="Edit section: Qatar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Qatar marked its first Qatar Children's day on 15 March 2018 &amp; it coincides with the date on which the Wudeema law (Child protection law) was issued.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
The Qatar also celebrates Universal Children's day on 20 November.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=88" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Children's Day was established in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> in 1954 by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a>, so as to create "a day of worldwide fraternity and understanding between children,"<sup id="cite_ref-National_Children&#39;s_Day_UK_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_Children&#39;s_Day_UK-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> although it is not widely celebrated. According to the National Children's Day UK website, Children's Day in the UK is not celebrated on the United Nation's nominated date of 20 November, so as to allow children the chance to go outside during summer on the day they are celebrated.<sup id="cite_ref-National_Children&#39;s_Day_UK_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_Children&#39;s_Day_UK-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=89" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Children's Day observations in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> predate both <a href="/wiki/Mother%27s_Day" title="Mother&#39;s Day">Mother's</a> and <a href="/wiki/Father%27s_Day" title="Father&#39;s Day">Father's Day</a>, though a permanent annual single Children's Day observation is not made at the national level.
</p><p>In 1856, Rev. Charles H. Leonard, D.D., then pastor of the First <a href="/wiki/Unitarian_Universalist_Association" title="Unitarian Universalist Association">Universalist Church</a> of <a href="/wiki/Chelsea,_Massachusetts" title="Chelsea, Massachusetts">Chelsea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Mass.</a>, set apart a Sunday for the dedication of children to the Christian life, and for the re-dedication of parents and guardians to bringing-up their children in Christian nurture. This service was first observed the second Sunday in June.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Unitarian_Universalist_Association" title="Unitarian Universalist Association">Universalist</a> Convention at Baltimore in September 1867, passed a resolution commending churches to set apart one Sunday in each year as Children's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-multiple_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-multiple-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Episcopal_Church" title="Methodist Episcopal Church">Methodist Episcopal Church</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Methodist" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist">Methodist</a> Conference of 1868 recommended that second Sunday in June be annually observed as Children's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-multiple_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-multiple-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The General Assembly of the <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_(U.S.A.)" class="mw-redirect" title="Presbyterian Church (U.S.A.)">Presbyterian Church</a> in 1883 designated "the second Sabbath in June as Children's Day."<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Also in 1883, the National Council of <a href="/wiki/Congregational_Churches" class="mw-redirect" title="Congregational Churches">Congregational Churches</a> and nearly all the state bodies of that denomination in the United States passed resolutions commending the observance of the day. About this time many other denominations adopted similar recommendations.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Chase's Calendar of Events</i> cites Children's Sunday and notes that The Commonwealth of Massachusetts issues an annual proclamation for the second Sunday in June.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Numerous churches and denominations currently observe the second Sunday in June including the <a href="/wiki/African_Methodist_Episcopal_Church" title="African Methodist Episcopal Church">African Methodist Episcopal Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_Methodist_Episcopal_Zion_Church" title="African Methodist Episcopal Zion Church">African Methodist Episcopal Zion Church</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Methodist_Episcopal_Church" title="Christian Methodist Episcopal Church">Christian Methodist Episcopal Church</a>.
</p><p>Children &amp; Youth Day in Hawaii started in 1994 when the Hawaii Legislature became the first to pass a law to recognize the first Sunday in October as "Children's Day". In 1997, the Legislature passed another landmark law designating the entire month of October as "Children and Youth Month".
</p><p>In 1996, author Pat Mora, after learning about the annual Mexican tradition of celebrating 30 April as El día del niño, the Day of the Child, proposed an annual celebration in the U.S. of El día de los niños, El día de los libros/Children's Day, Book Day, thus honoring children and connecting them to literacy, essential in a democracy.  Assistance starting this community-based, family literacy initiative was provided by REFORMA, the National Association to Promote Library &amp; Information Services to Latinos and the Spanish Speaking. Often known as Día, because it is both a daily commitment and an annual April celebration, Children's Day, Book Day, has grown to link all children to books, languages, and cultures. A major partner is the Association for Library Services to Children (ALSC), a division of the American Library Association (ALA). Every year, across the country, hundreds of libraries, schools, and community organizations, etc. hold culminating April Children's Day, Book Day celebrations that unite communities, creating an annual tradition much like Mother's Day and Father's Day.
</p><p>"National Children's Day" was proclaimed by President <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> to be held on 8 October 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> It was later designated by President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> as 3 June 2001, and in subsequent years on the first Sunday in June.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2009, Illinois Governor <a href="/wiki/Pat_Quinn_(politician)" title="Pat Quinn (politician)">Pat Quinn</a> has issued proclamations proclaiming the second Sunday in June as Children's Day as had the previous governor in 2007 and 2008. The mayors of Aurora and Batavia, Illinois, also have issued proclamations.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 23 April 2011, Executive of King County, WA declared 23 April as the International Children's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-childrensfest.tacawa.org_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-childrensfest.tacawa.org-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Children's Day celebrations of Turkish Community in California lead to the State of California recognizing the last Saturday of April as the Children's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dates">Dates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=90" title="Edit section: Dates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>2015: 2 August
</p><p>2016: 15 August
</p><p>2017: 30 June
</p><p>2018: 26 June
</p><p>2019: 9 June
</p><p>2020: 14 June
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Uruguay">Uruguay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=91" title="Edit section: Uruguay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Children's Day in <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a> is the second Sunday in August. 6 January is <a href="/wiki/Epiphany_(holiday)" title="Epiphany (holiday)">Epiphany (Reyes)</a>, also celebrated as Children's day.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=92" title="Edit section: Vanuatu">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a>, Children's Day is celebrated on 24 July. The two main themes of the holiday are "Stop violence against children" and "Give a child the chance to express their opinion today". After the march, there are speeches and activities organized by schools, including a dance. Then, after midday, children return home to spend time with their parents for the rest of the day. Children's Day is a public holiday, set up following a recommendation of the Committee on the Rights of the Child. A group of people in the United Nations monitor and protect children's rights. A committee, with both adult and child members, organizes activities. In the past, a committee of adults has chosen the theme – but in the future children may help choose it.
</p><p>Children's Day originally took place only in the capital of Vanuatu, but it has now been extended to all 6 provinces. Schools, churches, local governments of the provinces and other local organizations all organize activities. Save the Children supports one Children's Day activity in each province, selecting it from the many requests they receive for support. In 2008, one of the activities supported by Save the Children was a sports day between many different schools.
</p><p>Parents and caretakers have been supportive of Children's Day activities. Many parents come to activities with children. In one province, children and parents from five different schools came together for a shared lunch. Some parents give their children presents for Children's Day – however, Save the Children try to spread the message that it doesn't matter if a parent can't afford to buy their child a present, as the real aim of Children's Day is for parents and children to spend the day together, and work together to reconcile their problems.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Venezuela">Venezuela</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=93" title="Edit section: Venezuela">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, Children's Day is celebrated the third Sunday of July.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vietnam">Vietnam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=94" title="Edit section: Vietnam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Den_ong_sao.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Den_ong_sao.JPG/220px-Den_ong_sao.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Den_ong_sao.JPG/330px-Den_ong_sao.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Den_ong_sao.JPG/440px-Den_ong_sao.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Den_ong_sao.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mid-Autumn Festival in <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a></div></div></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, Children's Day is celebrated on 1 June as ICD and on the full moon of the 8th lunar month during the <a href="/wiki/Mid-Autumn_Festival" title="Mid-Autumn Festival">Mid-Autumn Festival</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Children%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=95" title="Edit section: Zimbabwe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Children's Day was established as a holiday in <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> in 1991 (<a href="/wiki/International_Day_of_the_African_Child" title="International Day of the African Child">Day of the African Child</a>).
</p>

<li id="cite_note-36"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-36">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">1923년 방정환(方定煥)을 포함한 일본유학생 모임인 '색동회’가 주축이 되어 5월 1일을 '어린이날’로 정하였다가 1927년 날짜를 5월 첫 일요일로 변경하였다.

</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div>
